This is information conceptually \"passed down\"\n    53→ * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"are we parsing strict code?\", and so\n    54→ * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\n    55→ *\n    56→ * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is like \"did we see a use strict\n    58→ * directive\"?\n    59→ *\n    60→ * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\n    61→ * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\n    62→ * information, and other such bits of data.\n    63→ *\n    64→ * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\n    65→ * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n    66→ * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n    67→ * can be optimized away.\n    68→ *\n    69→ * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n    70→ * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n    71→ * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\n    72→ * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\n    73→ * constructor's arguments).\n    74→ * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\n    75→ * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\n    76→ * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\n    77→ * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\n    78→ * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\n    79→ * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\n    80→ *\n    81→ * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\n    82→ *\n    83→ * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \"pass-down\"\n    84→ * data and some \"return-up\" data.\n    85→ *\n    86→ * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\n    87→ * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Certain limitations of\n * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\n * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\n * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\n * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\n *\n * == ParserSharedBase ==\n *\n * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\n * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\n * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\n * ParserBase type below.\n *\n * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\n *\n * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\n * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\n * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n *\n * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\n * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\n * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\n * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\n * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\n *\n * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\n *\n * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\n * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\n * to \"create an arguments object for a function\" obviously varies between\n * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\n * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\n * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\n *\n * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\n * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\n * further below).\n *\n * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\n *\n * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\n * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\n *\n *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\n *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\n *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\n *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\n *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\n *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\n *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\n *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\n *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\n *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\n *     character type.\n *\n * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\n * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\n *\n * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\n * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive.  As\n * noted above, this field's existence separate from that in ParserBase\n * motivates the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameters on various token stream\n * classes.\n *\n * Everything in PerHandlerParser *could* be folded into GeneralParser (below)\n * if desired.  We don't fold in this manner because all such functions would\n * be instantiated once per Unit -- but if exactly equivalent code would be\n * generated (because PerHandlerParser functions have no awareness of Unit),\n * it's risky to *depend* upon the compiler coalescing the instantiations into\n * one in the final binary.  PerHandlerParser guarantees no duplication.\n *\n * == Parser<ParseHandler, Unit> final → GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> ==\n *\n * The final (pun intended) axis of complexity lies in Parser.\n *","is_error":false}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3e44baa0-d91d-498a-829b-ced4729b29da","uuid":"e7835124-7f14-4ee5-9280-52f66363a469","tool_use_result":{"stdout":"/* -*- Mode: C++; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\n * vim: set ts=8 sts=2 et sw=2 tw=80:\n * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\n * License, v. 2.0. pipeline:\\n\\n**1. Entry Point - BytecodeCompiler (js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h/.cpp)**\\nPublic API functions like `CompileGlobalScript()`, `CompileEvalScript()`, and `CompileModule()` are the entry points. These functions initialize compilation state, create a ScriptCompiler instance, and orchestrate the entire parsing and compilation process. The main compilation routine is in `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate()` which delegates to `ScriptCompiler<Unit>::compile()`.\\n\\n**2. Parser Entry Point - Parser (js/src/frontend/Parser.h/.cpp)**\\nThe `Parser` class (and base `GeneralParser` class) implements the JavaScript parser. Key entry methods include:\\n- `globalBody(GlobalSharedContext*)` - parses global scope scripts\\n- `evalBody(EvalSharedContext*)` - parses eval scope scripts  \\n- These methods tokenize and parse source text, returning a `ParseNode` AST tree\\n\\n**3. AST Node Types - ParseNode (js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h)**\\nThe abstract syntax tree is represented by the `ParseNode` class hierarchy. All node types are defined through the `FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND` macro, which generates binary nodes (BinaryNode), unary nodes (UnaryNode), ternary nodes (TernaryNode), list nodes (ListNode), and specialized nodes like FunctionNode, ModuleNode, CallNode, etc. Each node type corresponds to JavaScript language constructs.\\n\\n**4. Bytecode Emission - BytecodeEmitter (js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h/.cpp)**\\nAfter parsing, the `BytecodeEmitter` class takes the ParseNode AST and generates bytecode. The main entry point is `emitScript(ParseNode* body)`. The emitter walks the AST and generates a sequence of bytecode instructions stored in `BytecodeSection`.
